3158

3159 <section id="_373">

3160

3161 <h2>

3162Treatment of Early Unfavorable Classic HL</h2>

3163

3164 <div id="_section_373" class="pdq-sections">

3165<nav class="in-this-section" role="navigation">

3166<h6>

3167In This Section</h6>

3168<ul>

3169<li>

3170<a href="#_1145_toc">

3171Treatment Options for Early Unfavorable Classic HL<ul>

3172<li>

3173<a href="#_924_toc">

3174Chemotherapy with or without radiation therapy</a>

3175</li>

3176</ul>

3177</a>

3178</li>

3179<li>

3180<a href="#_TrialSearch_373_sid_6_toc">

3181Current Clinical Trials</a>

3182</li>

3183</ul>

3184</nav>

3185<p id="_375" tabindex="-1">

3186Patients are designated as having early unfavorable classic Hodgkin lymphoma (HL) when they have clinical stage I or stage II disease and one or more of the following risk factors:</p>

3187<div class="pdq-content-list">

3188<ul id="_376">

3189<li>

3190B symptoms (unexplained fever &#8805;38&#176;C, soaking night sweats, unexplained weight loss &#8805;10% within 6 months). </li>

3191<li>

3192Extranodal disease.</li>

3193<li>

3194Bulky disease (&#8805;10 cm or &gt;33% of the chest diameter on chest x-ray).</li>

3195<li>

3196Three or more sites of nodal involvement.</li>

3197<li>

3198Sedimentation rate of 50 mm/h or higher.</li>

3199</ul>

3200</div>

3201<p id="_1155" tabindex="-1">

3202A retrospective review found that infradiaphragmatic early-stage disease appears to have an inferior outcome compared with the more frequent (&gt;90%) supradiaphragmatic disease, with a decrement in overall survival (OS) rates of 6% (91.5% vs. 97.6%; <em>

3203P</em>

3204 &lt; .001).[<a href="#cit/section_6.1">

32051</a>

3206][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810037&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810037&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

3207Level of evidence C2</a>

3208]</p>

3209<section id="_1145">

3210<h3 id="_1145_toc">

3211Treatment Options for Early Unfavorable Classic HL</h3>

3212<p id="_797" tabindex="-1">

3213Treatment options for early unfavorable classic HL include the following:</p>

3214<div class="pdq-content-list">

3215<ol id="_898">

3216<li>

3217<a href="/types/lymphoma/hp/adult-hodgkin-treatment-pdq#_924">

3218Chemotherapy with or without radiation therapy</a>

3219.</li>

3220</ol>

3221</div>

3222<section id="_924">

3223<h4 id="_924_toc">

3224Chemotherapy with or without radiation therapy</h4>

3225<p id="_925" tabindex="-1">

3226Treatment options include the following:[<a href="#cit/section_6.2">

32272</a>

3228,<a href="#cit/section_6.3">

32293</a>

3230]</p>

3231<div class="pdq-content-list">

3232<ul id="_799">

3233<li>

3234Four cycles of ABVD (doxorubicin, bleomycin, vinblastine, and dacarbazine) plus involved-field radiation therapy (IFRT) (20 Gy&#8211;30 Gy).[<a href="#cit/section_6.4">

32354</a>

3236-<a href="#cit/section_6.7">

32377</a>

3238]</li>

3239<li>

3240Six cycles of ABVD.[<a href="#cit/section_6.2">

32412</a>

3242,<a href="#cit/section_6.3">

32433</a>

3244]</li>

3245</ul>

3246</div>

3247<p id="_800" tabindex="-1">

3248See <a href="/types/lymphoma/hp/adult-hodgkin-treatment-pdq#_1152">

3249Table 4</a>

3250 for a description of the chemotherapy regimens used to treat HL.</p>

3251<p id="_801" tabindex="-1">

3252Evidence (chemotherapy and radiation therapy):</p>

3253<div class="pdq-content-list">

3254<ol id="_802">

3255<li>

3256A randomized, prospective trial from the National Cancer Institute of Canada (NCIC) involving 276 patients with early unfavorable HL compared ABVD for four to six cycles with ABVD for two cycles plus extended-field radiation therapy (EFRT).[<a href="#cit/section_6.2">

32572</a>

3258][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

3259Level of evidence A1</a>

3260]<div class="pdq-content-list">

3261<ul id="_803">

3262<li>

3263With a median follow-up of 11.3 years, the freedom from progression score favored combined-modality therapy (86% vs. 94%; <em>

3264P</em>

3265 = .006), but the OS rate was better for ABVD alone (92% vs. 81%; <em>

3266P</em>

3267 = .04).</li>

3268<li>

3269The trend toward a worse survival for the combined-modality arm was attributed to excess secondary malignancies and cardiovascular deaths. In this trial, the EFRT used higher doses and significantly larger exposure to body sites than are employed in current practice.</li>

3270<li>

3271This trial established that six cycles of ABVD can be used alone and that long-term complications from radiation therapy can negate differences for progression-free survival (PFS).</li>

3272</ul>

3273</div>

3274</li>

3275<li>

3276In the HD11 trial, the German Hodgkin Study Group (GHSG) randomly assigned 1,395 patients with early unfavorable HL to receive one of the following:<div class="pdq-content-list">

3277<ul id="_1149">

3278<li>

3279Four cycles of ABVD plus 30 Gy of IFRT.</li>

3280<li>

3281Four cycles of ABVD plus 20 Gy of IFRT.</li>

3282<li>

3283Four cycles of BEACOPP (bleomycin, etoposide, doxorubicin, cyclophosphamide, vincristine, procarbazine, and prednisone) plus 30 Gy of IFRT.</li>

3284<li>

3285Four cycles of BEACOPP plus 20 Gy of IFRT.</li>

3286</ul>

3287</div>

3288<p id="_808" tabindex="-1">

3289The following results were observed:</p>

3290<div class="pdq-content-list">

3291<ul id="_472">

3292<li>

3293With an 8.8-year median follow-up, no differences were observed in OS rates (93%&#8211;96%) for all four groups.[<a href="#cit/section_6.8">

32948</a>

3295][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

3296Level of evidence A1</a>

3297] </li>

3298<li>

3299In the study arms using 30 Gy of IFRT, there was no difference in freedom from treatment failure between BEACOPP and ABVD (<em>

3300P</em>

3301 = .65), but a significant difference against ABVD was seen for PFS when 20 Gy of IFRT was used (10-year PFS rate, 84% vs. 76%; hazard ratio (HR), 1.5; 95% confidence interval [CI], 1.0&#8211;2.1).[<a href="#cit/section_6.5">

33025</a>

3303][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

3304Level of evidence B1</a>

3305]</li>

3306<li>

3307In this trial, four cycles of ABVD plus 30 Gy of IFRT established this regimen as the preferred approach (or BEACOPP with 20 Gy of IFRT).</li>

3308</ul>

3309</div>

3310</li>

3311<li>

3312In the HD14 trial, the GHSG randomly assigned 1,528 patients with early unfavorable HL to receive either four cycles of ABVD plus 30 Gy of IFRT or two cycles of escalated BEACOPP followed by two cycles of ABVD plus 30 Gy of IFRT.[<a href="#cit/section_6.6">

33136</a>

3314][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

3315Level of evidence A1</a>

3316]<div class="pdq-content-list">

3317<ul id="_901">

3318<li>

3319With a median follow-up of 43 months, no difference was observed in OS.</li>

3320<li>

3321In this trial, four cycles of ABVD plus 30 Gy of IFRT established this regimen as the preferred approach.</li>

3322</ul>

3323</div>

3324</li>

3325<li>

3326In the H9-U trial, the European Organisation for Research and Treatment of Cancer&#8211;Groupe d'&#201;tude des Lymphomes de l'Adulte (EORTC/GELA) randomly assigned 808 patients with early unfavorable disease (including 40% with bulky disease) to receive one of the following [<a href="#cit/section_6.7">

33277</a>

3328][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

3329Level of evidence A1</a>

3330]:<div class="pdq-content-list">

3331<ul id="_1150">

3332<li>

3333Six cycles of ABVD plus 36 Gy of IFRT.</li>

3334<li>

3335Four cycles of ABVD plus 36 Gy of IFRT.</li>

3336<li>

3337Four cycles of BEACOPP plus 36 Gy of IFRT.</li>

3338</ul>

3339</div>

3340<p id="_1009" tabindex="-1">

3341The following results were observed:</p>

3342<div class="pdq-content-list">

3343<ul id="_1010">

3344<li>

3345With a median follow-up of 64 months, no differences were observed (event-free survival rates, 89%&#8211;92%; <em>

3346P</em>

3347 = .38; or OS rates, 91%&#8211;96%; <em>

3348P</em>

3349 = .89).</li>

3350<li>

3351Based on toxicities, four cycles of ABVD plus IFRT was established as the preferred regimen.</li>

3352</ul>

3353</div>

3354</li>

3355<li>

3356A multicenter nonrandomized study in 117 patients (most of whom had bulky disease) showed that four cycles of A+AVD (brentuximab vedotin + doxorubicin, vinblastine, and dacarbazine) with or without involved-site radiation therapy is well-tolerated and effective.[<a href="#cit/section_6.9">

33579</a>

3358]<div class="pdq-content-list">

3359<ul id="_1315">

3360<li>

3361With a median follow-up of 3.8 years, the overall 2-year PFS was 94% (95% CI, 89.7%&#8211;98.3%). The 2-year OS was 99.1% (97.3%&#8211; 100.0%).[<a href="#cit/section_6.9">

33629</a>

3363][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810037&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810037&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

3364Level of evidence C2</a>

3365]</li>

3366<li>

3367This pilot study requires confirmation, but the results may be reassuring when using the regimen for patients who cannot take bleomycin or need to limit anthracycline exposure.</li>

3368</ul>

3369</div>

3370</li>

3371</ol>

3372</div>

3373<p id="_810" tabindex="-1">

3374<strong>

3375Could the radiation therapy be omitted to minimize late morbidity and mortality from secondary solid tumors and from cardiovascular disease?</strong>

3376[<a href="#cit/section_6.3">

33773</a>

3378] </p>

3379<div class="pdq-content-list">

3380<ul id="_1139" class="pdq-address-block">

3381<li>

3382The NCIC study addressed this question in patients with early unfavorable HL. Although four to six cycles of ABVD alone had improved OS compared with a combined-modality approach, the use of EFRT in the combined-modality arm is excessive by current standards, and late effects will be magnified with these larger fields.[<a href="#cit/section_6.2">

33832</a>

3384] In addition, chemotherapy alone was 8% worse in freedom from disease progression compared with the combined-modality approach. An indirect comparison for using ABVD alone is that the 94% OS rate reported for patients with early unfavorable HL in the NCIC study [<a href="#cit/section_6.2">

33852</a>

3386] at 11 years is equivalent to the survival reported at 11 years in the GHSG's <a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT02495922">

3387HD6</a>

3388 (NCT00002561), <a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT00265018">

3389HD10</a>

3390 (NCT01399931), and <a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT00264953">

3391HD11</a>

3392 (NCT0264953) trials using combined-modality therapy.[<a href="#cit/section_6.10">

339310</a>

3394] In addition, for the HD6 and HD10 trials, between the reports at 55 months and subsequently at 133 months, cardiovascular events doubled and solid tumor events tripled.[<a href="#cit/section_6.10">

339510</a>

3396]</li>

3397<li>

3398A retrospective analysis of 215 patients treated with ABVD and more contemporary radiation therapy (20 Gy&#8211;30 Gy, limited field) was compared with a cohort of 860 individuals matched for age, sex, geographical region, and major medical diseases.[<a href="#cit/section_6.11">

339911</a>

3400] Excess morbidity was still seen in terms of second malignancies, cardiovascular disease, and respiratory disease (HR, 1.5&#8211;7.6), but at a lower rate than in reports using regimens and doses from earlier decades.[<a href="#cit/section_6.11">

340111</a>

3402]</li>

3403</ul>

3404</div>

3405<p id="_423" tabindex="-1">

3406A Cochrane meta-analysis of 1,245 patients in five randomized clinical trials suggested improved survival for combined-modality therapy versus chemotherapy alone (HR, 0.40; 95% CI, 0.27&#8211;0.61).[<a href="#cit/section_6.12">

340712</a>

3408] However, the five randomized trials that were analyzed had inadequate follow-up to account for the late toxicities and increased mortality seen with radiation therapy after 10 years. </p>

3409<p id="_1011" tabindex="-1">

3410<strong>

3411Other trials have investigated the role of positron emission tomography&#8210;computed tomography (PET-CT) scans for patients with early unfavorable HL.</strong>

3412</p>

3413<div class="pdq-content-list">

3414<ol id="_1130">

3415<li>

3416A randomized prospective trial (EORTC HIOU) of 1,196 patients with early unfavorable HL investigated the use of PET-CT scans to modify therapy after two cycles of therapy.[<a href="#cit/section_6.13">

341713</a>

3418]<div class="pdq-content-list">

3419<ol id="_1151" class="lower-alpha">

3420<li>

3421Among the 815 patients with negative PET-CT findings (Deauville score of 1 or 2) after two cycles of ABVD, the patients randomly assigned to receive six cycles of ABVD had inferior PFS rates compared with patients who received four cycles of ABVD plus involved nodal radiation therapy (94.7% vs. 99.2%; <em>

3422P</em>

3423 = .026), but no difference in OS.[<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

3424Level of evidence B1</a>

3425]</li>

3426<li>

3427The use of ABVD for six cycles is acceptable in the absence of radiation therapy for patients with early unfavorable classic HL who have negative PET-CT results after two cycles of ABVD, if one can accept a 5% rate of increased relapse, with no decrement in OS after salvage therapy.</li>

3428<li>

3429In a follow-up report from this trial, 381 patients with positive PET-CT results (Deauville score of 3, 4, or 5) after two cycles of ABVD were randomly assigned to receive four cycles of ABVD plus 30 Gy of involved nodal radiation therapy versus two cycles of ABVD followed by two cycles of escalated BEACOPP plus 30 Gy of involved nodal radiation therapy.[<a href="#cit/section_6.14">

343014</a>

3431][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

3432Level of evidence A1</a>

3433]<div class="pdq-content-list">

3434<ul id="_1132">

3435<li>

3436The 5-year PFS rate was 91% in the BEACOPP arm compared with 77% in the ABVD arm (<em>

3437P</em>

3438 = .002).</li>

3439<li>

3440The 5-year OS rate was 96% in the BEACOPP arm compared with 89% in the ABVD arm (<em>

3441P</em>

3442 = .02).</li>

3443</ul>

3444</div>

3445</li>

3446</ol>

3447</div>

3448<p id="_1267" tabindex="-1">

3449This trial supports adding escalated BEACOPP to ABVD for patients with early unfavorable classic HL who have positive PET-CT results after two cycles.</p>

3450</li>

3451<li>

3452A randomized prospective trial (<a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT01356680">

3453GHSG HD17</a>

3454 [NCT01356680]) of 1,100 patients with early-stage unfavorable HL evaluated whether radiation therapy can be omitted in patients with a complete metabolic response (CMR) on PET-CT scan after two cycles of escalated BEACOPP and two cycles of regular-dose BEACOPP (2 + 2 regimen). Patients were randomly assigned to receive combined-modality therapy (n = 548) or PET4-guided therapy (n = 552). Combined-modality therapy included both the 2 + 2 regimen and involved-field radiation therapy. PET4-guided therapy included the 2 + 2 regimen for all patients and involved-node radiation therapy for the patients with a positive PET4 scan (n = 160). A total of 333 patients in the PET4-guided therapy group were PET4-negative and received chemotherapy alone.[<a href="#cit/section_6.15">

345515</a>

3456]<div class="pdq-content-list">

3457<ul id="_1268">

3458<li>

3459With a median follow-up of 46.2 months, the 5-year PFS rate was 97.3% (95% CI, 94.5%&#8211;98.7%) for patients who received combined-modality therapy and 95.1% (95% CI, 92.0%&#8211;97.0%) for patients who received PET4-guided therapy (HR, 0.523; 95% CI, 0.23&#8211;1.21). The between-group difference was 2.2% (95% CI, -0.9% to 5.3%) and excluded the noninferiority margin of 8%.[<a href="#cit/section_6.15">

346015</a>

3461][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

3462Level of evidence B1</a>

3463]</li>

3464<li>

3465In the subgroup of PET4-negative patients who received chemotherapy alone, the difference in 5-year PFS was 1.7% (95% CI, -1.8% to 5.3%).</li>

3466<li>

3467Omitting radiation therapy for patients in CMR after four cycles of BEACOPP-based chemotherapy did not significantly impair PFS.</li>

3468</ul>

3469</div>

3470</li>

3471<li>

3472A prospective phase II trial included 94 patients with early-stage (I/II) bulky disease (defined as mass &gt;10 cm or &gt;&#8531; maximum intrathoracic diameter on chest x-ray). Patients received ABVD for two cycles, followed by interim PET (PET2) scan. PET-negative patients (78% of the total) were defined as Deauville 1, 2, or 3 and received two more cycles of ABVD. PET2-positive patients (Deauville 4 or 5, 22% of the total) received four cycles of escalated BEACOPP, followed by 30.6 Gy of IFRT.[<a href="#cit/section_6.16">

347316</a>

3474]<div class="pdq-content-list">

3475<ul id="_1330">

3476<li>

3477With a median follow-up of 60 months, the 3-year PFS rate was 93.1% in PET2-negative patients and 89.7% in PET2-positive patients. The 3-year OS rate was 98.6% in PET2-negative patients and 94.4% in PET2-positive patients.[<a href="#cit/section_6.16">

347816</a>

3479][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810039&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810039&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

3480Level of evidence C3</a>

3481]</li>

3482</ul>

3483</div>

3484</li>

3485</ol>

3486</div>

3487<p id="_1015" tabindex="-1">

3488To summarize: </p>

3489<div class="pdq-content-list">

3490<ul id="_1123">

3491<li>

3492Most of the trials support using four cycles of ABVD plus 30 Gy of IFRT or involved nodal radiation therapy.[<a href="#cit/section_6.17">

349317</a>

3494] </li>

3495<li>

3496ABVD alone for six cycles is a reasonable alternative despite a 5% to 6% decrement in PFS because the long-term toxicities of adding radiation therapy will affect OS, which is the most important patient outcome.[<a href="#cit/section_6.17">

349717</a>

3498] </li>

3499<li>

3500For patients with a positive PET-CT (usually Deauville 4 or 5) after two cycles of ABVD, adding brentuximab vedotin while eliminating bleomycin can be considered. BEACOPP or clinical trials investigating the addition of brentuximab vedotin or checkpoint inhibitors in this setting would be indicated.</li>

3501<li>

3502Radiation therapy may be omitted in patients with a negative PET-CT (Deauville 1) after two to four cycles of chemotherapy.</li>

3503</ul>

3504</div>

3505<p id="_389" tabindex="-1">

3506Patients with bulky disease (&#8805;10 cm) or massive mediastinal involvement were excluded from most of the trials. On the basis of historical comparisons to chemotherapy or radiation therapy alone, these patients receive combined-modality therapy.[<a href="#cit/section_6.18">

350718</a>

3508-<a href="#cit/section_6.20">

350920</a>

3510][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810037&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810037&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

3511Level of evidence C2</a>

3512] A retrospective review published in a preliminary abstract reported on 194 patients with bulky disease who had PET-CT scans at the completion of chemotherapy; 112 of them had negative PET results (Deauville score of 1 or 2).[<a href="#cit/section_6.21">

351321</a>

3514] The observed 86% OS rate at 5 years suggests that radiation therapy can be excluded for patients with massive mediastinal disease who have negative PET-CT scan results after six cycles of therapy.[<a href="#cit/section_6.21">

351521</a>

3516][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810037&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810037&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

3517Level of evidence C2</a>

3518]</p>

3519</section>

3520</section>

3527 to find NCI-supported cancer clinical trials that are now enrolling patients. 3625 <h2>

3626Treatment of Advanced Classic HL</h2>

3627

3628 <div id="_section_402" class="pdq-sections">

3629<nav class="in-this-section" role="navigation">

3631In This Section</h6>

3635Treatment Options for Advanced Classic HL<ul>

3641</a>

3649<p id="_909" tabindex="-1">

3650The following adverse prognostic factors for advanced classic Hodgkin lymphoma (HL) have been combined into the International Prognostic Score for advanced-stage HL:[<a href="#cit/section_7.1">

36511</a>

3652]</p>

3653<div class="pdq-content-list">

3654<ul id="_910">

3655<li>

3656 Albumin level lower than 4.0 g/L.</li>

3657<li>

3658Hemoglobin level lower than 10.5 g/L.</li>

3659<li>

3660Male sex.</li>

3661<li>

3662Age 45 years or older.</li>

3663<li>

3664Stage IV disease.</li>

3665<li>

3666White blood cell (WBC) count of 15,000/mm<span class="sup">

36673</span>

3668 or higher.</li>

3669<li>

3670Absolute lymphocyte count lower than 600/mm<span class="sup">

36713</span>

3672 or a lymphocyte count higher than 8% of the total WBC count.</li>

3673</ul>

3750<p id="_1016" tabindex="-1">

3751Even the highest-risk patients in this index have a 5-year freedom from progression rate above 60% and a 5-year overall survival (OS) rate above 70%.[<a href="#cit/section_7.1">

37521</a>

3753]</p>

3754<section id="_1146">

3755<h3 id="_1146_toc">

3756Treatment Options for Advanced Classic HL</h3>

3757<p id="_820" tabindex="-1">

3758Treatment options for advanced classic HL include the following:</p>

3759<div class="pdq-content-list">

3760<ol id="_911">

3761<li>

3762<a href="/types/lymphoma/hp/adult-hodgkin-treatment-pdq#_930">

3763Chemotherapy</a>

3764.</li>

3765</ol>

3766</div>

3767<section id="_930">

3768<h4 id="_930_toc">

3769Chemotherapy</h4>

3770<p id="_931" tabindex="-1">

3771The chemotherapy regimen A+AVD (brentuximab vedotin [an antibody-drug conjugate directed against CD30] + doxorubicin, vinblastine, and dacarbazine) is administered for six cycles. This replaces ABVD (doxorubicin, bleomycin, vinblastine, and dacarbazine), the previous standard regimen for three decades.[<a href="#cit/section_7.2">

37722</a>

3773,<a href="#cit/section_7.3">

37743</a>

3775] The ABVD regimen remains a viable option in cost-conscious settings.</p>

3776<p id="_823" tabindex="-1">

3777See <a href="/types/lymphoma/hp/adult-hodgkin-treatment-pdq#_1152">

3778Table 4 </a>

3779for a description of the chemotherapy regimens used to treat HL.</p>

3780<p id="_1133" tabindex="-1">

3781Evidence (chemotherapy):</p>

3782<div class="pdq-content-list">

3783<ol id="_1140">

3784<li>

3785A randomized prospective trial (<a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT01712490">

3786NCT01712490</a>

3787) included 1,334 patients with previously untreated advanced-stage HL. The study compared ABVD with A+AVD (a regimen substituting brentuximab vedotin for bleomycin).[<a href="#cit/section_7.4">

37884</a>

3789]<div class="pdq-content-list">

3790<ul id="_1306">

3791<li>

3792With a median follow-up of 73 months, the 6-year OS rate was 93.9% for patients who received A+AVD (95% confidence interval [CI], 91.6%&#8211;95.5%) and 89.4% for patients who received ABVD (95% CI, 86.6%&#8211;91.7%) (hazard ratio [HR], 0.59; 95% CI, 0.40&#8211;0.88; <em>

3793P</em>

3794 = .009).[<a href="#cit/section_7.4">

37954</a>

3796]</li>

3797<li>

3798With a median follow-up of 73 months, the 6-year progression-free survival (PFS) rate was 82.3% for patients who received A+AVD (95% CI, 79.1%&#8211;85.0%) and 74.5% for patients who received ABVD (95% CI, 70.8%&#8211;77.7%) (HR, 0.68; 95% CI, 0.53&#8211;0.86; <em>

3799P</em>

3800 = .002).[<a href="#cit/section_7.4">

38014</a>

3802]</li>

3803<li>

3804Among patients who received A+AVD, there was significantly more grade 3 or 4 peripheral neuropathy (67% vs. 43%); however, there was more than 80% partial or complete recovery, with a median time-to-resolution of 16 weeks for A+AVD and 10 weeks for ABVD. Pulmonary toxicity led to 11 deaths in the ABVD arm.</li>

3805<li>

3806Although fertility was not directly assessed, pregnancies and live births subsequently occurred in both arms of the trial for female patients and female partners of the male patients.</li>

3807<li>

3808A+AVD can cost 50 times more than ABVD (in 2018).[<a href="#cit/section_7.5">

38095</a>

3810]</li>

3811</ul>

3812</div>

3813</li>

3814<li>

3815In multiple prospective trials and a meta-analysis, ABVD therapy for 6 to 8 months remains the standard of care for patients with advanced HL, with equivalent OS when compared with other regimens (i.e., BEACOPP [bleomycin, etoposide, doxorubicin, cyclophosphamide, vincristine, procarbazine, and prednisone], escalated BEACOPP, Stanford V [doxorubicin, vinblastine, mechlorethamine, etoposide, vincristine, bleomycin, and prednisone], and MOPP-ABV [mechlorethamine, vincristine, procarbazine prednisone/doxorubicin, bleomycin, and vinblastine]).[<a href="#cit/section_7.6">

38166</a>

3817-<a href="#cit/section_7.13">

381813</a>

3819][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

3820Level of evidence A1</a>

3821]</li>

3822</ol>

3823</div>

3824<p id="_1017" tabindex="-1">

3825<strong>

3826Multiple studies have addressed the role of radiation therapy consolidation after induction chemotherapy for advanced-stage HL.</strong>

3827</p>

3828<div class="pdq-content-list">

3829<ol id="_1134">

3830<li>

3831Three prospective randomized trials did not show a benefit

3832in OS from the addition of consolidative radiation therapy to

3833chemotherapy for patients with advanced-stage disease.[<a href="#cit/section_7.14">

383414</a>

3835-<a href="#cit/section_7.16">

383616</a>

3837][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

3838Level of evidence A1</a>

3839]</li>

3840<li>

3841In a meta-analysis

3842of 1,740 patients treated in 14 different trials, no improvement was observed in

384310-year OS for patients with advanced-stage HL who

3844received combined-modality therapy compared with chemotherapy alone.[<a href="#cit/section_7.17">

384517</a>

3846][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810035&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810035&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

3847Level of evidence C1</a>

3848] </li>

3849<li>

3850No survival advantage is known for the use of radiation consolidation for patients with massive mediastinal disease and advanced-stage disease.[<a href="#cit/section_7.18">

385118</a>

3852]<p id="_1269" tabindex="-1">

3853A randomized prospective trial with a median follow-up of 5.9 years included 320 patients with advanced-stage HL and a large nodal mass (&#8805;5 cm). Patients were randomly assigned to receive radiation therapy or no further treatment after six cycles of ABVD. For patients with a complete metabolic response on positron emission tomography (PET)&#8211;computed tomography (CT) after six cycles of ABVD, there was no difference in the 6-year PFS rate for patients who received radiation therapy (91%; 95% CI, 84%&#8211;99%) versus patients who received no further treatment (95%; 95% CI, 89%&#8211;100%, <em>

3854P</em>

3855 = .62).[<a href="#cit/section_7.19">

385619</a>

3857][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

3858Level of evidence B1</a>

3859]</p>

3860</li>

3861<li>

3862The German Hodgkin Lymphoma Study Group HD15 trial showed that a negative PET scan after induction therapy with BEACOPP (escalated or every 14 days) for advanced-stage HL was highly predictive for a good outcome, even with the omission of consolidative radiation therapy (negative predictive value for PET was 94% [95% CI, 91%&#8211;97%]).[<a href="#cit/section_7.20">

386320</a>

3864] In the German Hodgkin Study Group <a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT00515554">

3865HD18</a>

3866 trial (NCT00515554), PET scan negativity after two cycles (PET2) of escalated BEACOPP allowed reduction to four cycles of therapy instead of six or eight cycles because of the equivalent 5-year PFS (90.8% vs. 92.2%; difference 1.4%; 95% CI, -2.7&#8211;5.4).[<a href="#cit/section_7.21">

386721</a>

3868][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

3869Level of evidence B1</a>

3870] The HD18 trial established a Deauville score of 4 or 5 as PET2 positive based on a 3-year OS.[<a href="#cit/section_7.22">

387122</a>

3872]</li>

3873</ol>

3874</div>

3875<p id="_1135" tabindex="-1">

3876<strong>

3877Other trials have investigated the role of PET scans patients with advanced classic HL.</strong>

3878</p>

3879<div class="pdq-content-list">

3880<ol id="_1136">

3881<li>

3882A randomized prospective trial of 1,214 patients with advanced-stage HL (<a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT00678327">

3883RATHL</a>

3884 [NCT00678327]) investigated the use of PET-CT scans after two cycles of ABVD to modify therapy.[<a href="#cit/section_7.23">

388523</a>

3886] Patients with negative findings from a PET-CT scan (Deauville score of 1, 2, or 3) were randomly assigned to receive four more cycles of ABVD versus four cycles of AVD (doxorubicin, vinblastine, and dacarbazine).<div class="pdq-content-list">

3887<ol id="_1194" class="lower-alpha">

3888<li>

3889With a median follow-up of 41 months for the 937 patients with negative PET-CT results, there was no difference in the 3-year OS rate (97.2%; 95% CI, 95.1%&#8211;98.4% for ABVD vs. 97.6%; 95% CI, 95.6%&#8211;98.7% for AVD).[<a href="#cit/section_7.23">

389023</a>

3891][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

3892Level of evidence A1</a>

3893]</li>

3894<li>

3895The absolute difference in the 3-year PFS (ABVD minus AVD) was 1.6% (95% CI, -3.2 to 5.3), which was just over the specified nonsuperiority margin. This means that there was a small advantage for continuing bleomycin because of PFS.</li>

3896<li>

3897However, pulmonary toxicity was worse in the continued ABVD arm, with significantly more grade 3 or 4 respiratory events and worsened long-term diffusing capacity of the lung for carbon monoxide levels persisting beyond 1 year.</li>

3898<li>

3899This study concluded that bleomycin may be omitted after the second cycle of ABVD if findings from the PET-CT scan are negative (Deauville score of 1, 2, or 3).</li>

3900<li>

3901The patients with positive PET-CT scan results (Deauville score of 4 or 5) after two cycles of ABVD received BEACOPP.<div class="pdq-content-list">

3902<ul id="_1195">

3903<li>

3904With a median follow-up of 41 months for the 172 patients with positive PET-CT results, the 3-year PFS rate was 67.5% and the OS rate was 87.8%</li>

3905<li>

3906This trial did not establish that switching to BEACOPP was superior to remaining on ABVD.</li>

3907</ul>

3908</div>

3909</li>

3910</ol>

3911</div>

3912</li>

3913<li>

3914In a nonrandomized trial (<a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT00822120">

3915SWOG S0816</a>

3916 [NCT00822120]), 336 patients with advanced HL received two cycles of ABVD and then were evaluated by PET scan.[<a href="#cit/section_7.24">

391724</a>

3918] PET2&#8211;negative patients (Deauville score of 1 to 3) completed four more cycles of ABVD, while the 60 PET2&#8211;positive patients (18% of total) were switched to escalated BEACOPP. <div class="pdq-content-list">

3919<ul id="_1196">

3920<li>

3921With a median follow-up of 5.9 years, the 5-year PFS rate for the PET2&#8211;positive patients was 66% (95% CI, 52%&#8211;76%).[<a href="#cit/section_7.24">

392224</a>

3923][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810039&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810039&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

3924Level of evidence C3</a>

3925]</li>

3926</ul>

3927</div>

3928</li>

3929</ol>

3930</div>

3931<p id="_1242" tabindex="-1">

3932<strong>

3933Older patients with advanced-stage HL have also been studied.</strong>

3934</p>

3935<div class="pdq-content-list">

3936<ol id="_1243">

3937<li>

3938In a multicenter phase II study, 48 patients older than 60 years, of whom 81% had advanced-stage disease, received brentuximab vedotin for two consecutive doses, followed by six cycles of AVD, followed by four more doses of brentuximab vedotin.[<a href="#cit/section_7.25">

393925</a>

3940]<div class="pdq-content-list">

3941<ul id="_1244">

3942<li>

3943The 2-year event-free survival rate was 80%, PFS rate was 84%, and OS rate was 93%.[<a href="#cit/section_7.25">

394425</a>

3945][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810039&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810039&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

3946Level of evidence C3</a>

3947]</li>

3948<li>

3949Grade 3 or 4 toxicity was experienced by 42% of patients.</li>

3950</ul>

3951</div>

3952</li>

3953</ol>

3954</div>

3955<p id="_1245" tabindex="-1">

3956<strong>

3957Summary of advanced-stage classic HL:</strong>

3958</p>

3959<div class="pdq-content-list">

3960<ul id="_1124">

3961<li>

3962For patients with advanced-stage HL, six cycles of ABVD is the standard approach. In situations in which use of bleomycin is contraindicated, A+AVD is a good option.</li>

3963<li>

3964For patients with negative PET-CT scan results after the second cycle of ABVD, bleomycin may be omitted from the chemotherapy regimen with little loss of efficacy and improvement in tolerability.</li>

3965</ul>

3966</div>

3967</section>

3968</section>

4059Kobe C, Dietlein M, Franklin J, et al.: Positron emission tomography has a high negative predictive value for progression or early relapse for patients with residual disease after first-line chemotherapy in advanced-stage Hodgkin lymphoma. Blood 112 (10): 3989-94, 2008.&#160;<a href="http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/entrez/query.fcgi?cmd=Retrieve&amp;db=PubMed&amp;list_uids=18757777&amp;dopt=Abstract" title="http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/entrez/query.fcgi?cmd=Retrieve&amp;db=PubMed&amp;list_uids=18757777&amp;dopt=Abstract">

Lancet 390 (10114): 2790-2802, 2018.&#160;<a href="http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/entrez/query.fcgi?cmd=Retrieve&amp;db=PubMed&amp;list_uids=29061295&amp;dopt=Abstract" title="http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/entrez/query.fcgi?cmd=Retrieve&amp;db=PubMed&amp;list_uids=29061295&amp;dopt=Abstract">

4089 <section id="_174">

4090

4091 <h2>

4092Treatment of Recurrent Classic HL</h2>

4093

4094 <div id="_section_174" class="pdq-sections">

4095<nav class="in-this-section" role="navigation">

4096<h6>

4097In This Section</h6>

4098<ul>

4099<li>

4100<a href="#_1147_toc">

4101Treatment Options for Recurrent Classic HL<ul>

4102<li>

4103<a href="#_1270_toc">

4104Nivolumab or pembrolizumab</a>

4105</li>

4106<li>

4107<a href="#_1047_toc">

4108Brentuximab vedotin</a>

4109</li>

4110<li>

4111<a href="#_1283_toc">

4112Brentuximab vedotin plus nivolumab</a>

4113</li>

4114<li>

4115<a href="#_1083_toc">

4116Chemotherapy with stem cell transplant</a>

4117</li>

4118<li>

4119<a href="#_933_toc">

4120Combination chemotherapy</a>

4121</li>

4122<li>

4123<a href="#_937_toc">

4124Radiation therapy</a>

4125</li>

4126<li>

4127<a href="#_1076_toc">

4128Summary for sequencing therapies for recurrent classic HL</a>

4129</li>

4130</ul>

4131</a>

4132</li>

4133<li>

4134<a href="#_TrialSearch_174_sid_8_toc">

4135Current Clinical Trials</a>

4136</li>

4137</ul>

4138</nav>

4139<p id="_1043" tabindex="-1">

4140More than half of all patients with recurrent Hodgkin lymphoma (HL) can achieve long-term disease-free survival (DFS), or even cure, using reinduction therapy followed by stem cell/bone marrow transplant consolidation.[<a href="#cit/section_8.1">

41411</a>

4142] In this regard, the disease follows a <em>

414375%</em>

4144<em>

4145 rule</em>

4146: 75% of patients attain a clinical complete remission with salvage therapy reinduction, and then 75% of patients who undergo autologous stem cell transplant (SCT) are free of disease at 4 years. Poor prognostic factors include the following:[<a href="#cit/section_8.2">

41472</a>

4148-<a href="#cit/section_8.4">

41494</a>

4150]</p>

4151<div class="pdq-content-list">

4152<ul id="_1044">

4153<li>

4154Primary refractory disease (worst prognosis).</li>

4155<li>

4156Relapse less than 12 months after initial therapy. Among patients who initially present with early-stage favorable disease that relapses, more than 75% have a relapse more than 12 months after diagnosis.[<a href="#cit/section_8.5">

41575</a>

4158]</li>

4159<li>

4160Inability to attain a clinical complete remission after reinduction (i.e., positron emission tomography&#8210;computed tomography [PET-CT] scan results are positive with a Deauville score of 4 or 5 followed by subsequent progression in the size and/or sites of disease).</li>

4161<li>

4162 <a href="/types/lymphoma/hp/adult-hodgkin-treatment-pdq#_966">

4163B symptoms</a>

4164 at relapse.</li>

4165<li>

4166Extranodal disease at relapse.</li>

4167<li>

4168More than two previous salvage regimens received.</li>

4169</ul>

4170</div>

4171<section id="_1147">

4172<h3 id="_1147_toc">

4173Treatment Options for Recurrent Classic HL</h3>

4174<p id="_1045" tabindex="-1">

4175Treatment options for recurrent classic HL:</p>

4176<div class="pdq-content-list">

4177<ol id="_1046">

4178<li>

4179<a href="/types/lymphoma/hp/adult-hodgkin-treatment-pdq#_1270">

4180Nivolumab or pembrolizumab</a>

4181.</li>

4182<li>

4183<a href="/types/lymphoma/hp/adult-hodgkin-treatment-pdq#_1047">

4184Brentuximab vedotin</a>

4185.</li>

4186<li>

4187<a href="/types/lymphoma/hp/adult-hodgkin-treatment-pdq#_1283">

4188Brentuximab vedotin plus nivolumab</a>

4189.</li>

4190<li>

4191<a href="/types/lymphoma/hp/adult-hodgkin-treatment-pdq#_1083">

4192Chemotherapy with stem cell transplant</a>

4193.</li>

4194<li>

4195<a href="/types/lymphoma/hp/adult-hodgkin-treatment-pdq#_933">

4196Combination chemotherapy</a>

4197.</li>

4198<li>

4199<a href="/types/lymphoma/hp/adult-hodgkin-treatment-pdq#_937">

4200Radiation therapy</a>

4201.</li>

4202</ol>

4203</div>

4204<section id="_1270">

4205<h4 id="_1270_toc">

4206Nivolumab or pembrolizumab</h4>

4207<p id="_1271" tabindex="-1">

4208The anti-programmed cell death-1 (PD-1) monoclonal antibodies nivolumab and pembrolizumab are immune checkpoint inhibitors.</p>

4209<p id="_1272" tabindex="-1">

4210Evidence: (pembrolizumab):</p>

4211<div class="pdq-content-list">

4212<ol id="_1273">

4213<li>

4214A prospective randomized trial included 304 patients with relapsed or refractory disease who were ineligible for or had a relapse after autologous SCT. Patients were assigned to receive either pembrolizumab or brentuximab vedotin.[<a href="#cit/section_8.6">

42156</a>

4216]<div class="pdq-content-list">

4217<ul id="_1274">

4218<li>

4219With a median follow-up of 25.7 months, the median progression-free survival (PFS) for patients who received pembrolizumab was 13.2 months (95% confidence interval [CI], 10.9&#8211;19.4) versus 8.3 months (95% CI, 5.7&#8211;8.8) for patients who received brentuximab vedotin (hazard ratio [HR], 0.65; 95% CI, 0.48&#8211;0.88; <em>

4220P</em>

4221 = .0027).[<a href="#cit/section_8.6">

42226</a>

4223][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

4224Level of evidence B1</a>

4225]</li>

4226<li>

4227Serious treatment-related adverse events occurred in 16% of patients who received pembrolizumab and 11% of patients who received brentuximab vedotin.</li>

4228</ul>

4229</div>

4230</li>

4231<li>

4232Studies of patients with relapsed HL treated with pembrolizumab reported the following:[<a href="#cit/section_8.7">

42337</a>

4234,<a href="#cit/section_8.8">

42358</a>

4236][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810039&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810039&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

4237Level of evidence C3</a>

4238]<div class="pdq-content-list">

4239<ul id="_1275">

4240<li>

4241The overall response rate was 64% to 74%, with a complete response rate of 22.4% (95% CI, 6.9%&#8211;28.6%).</li>

4242<li>

4243Pembrolizumab was well tolerated by patients and can be used to achieve a clinical complete remission before autologous or allogeneic SCT.</li>

4244<li>

4245The U.S. Food and Drug Administration (FDA) approved pembrolizumab for use in cases of refractory disease or relapse after three or more lines of therapy.</li>

4246</ul>

4247</div>

4248</li>

4249<li>

4250A phase II trial included 39 patients with transplant-eligible relapsed or refractory disease. Patients received pembrolizumab with GVD chemotherapy (gemcitabine, vinorelbine, and liposomal doxorubicin).[<a href="#cit/section_8.9">

42519</a>

4252]<div class="pdq-content-list">

4253<ul id="_1316">

4254<li>

4255With a median follow-up of 13.5 months, the overall response rate was 100%, and the complete response rate was 95%.[<a href="#cit/section_8.9">

42569</a>

4257][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810039&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810039&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

4258Level of evidence C3</a>

4259]</li>

4260<li>

4261Thirty-six patients (35%) proceeded to autologous SCT consolidation.</li>

4262</ul>

4263</div>

4264</li>

4265</ol>

4266</div>

4267<p id="_1276" tabindex="-1">

4268Evidence (nivolumab):</p>

4269<div class="pdq-content-list">

4270<ol id="_1277">

4271<li>

4272Studies of patients with relapsed HL treated with nivolumab reported the following:[<a href="#cit/section_8.10">

427310</a>

4274-<a href="#cit/section_8.12">

427512</a>

4276][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810039&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810039&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

4277Level of evidence C3</a>

4278]<div class="pdq-content-list">

4279<ul id="_1278">

4280<li>

4281The overall response rate was 65% to 87% and the complete response rate was 16% to 28%, with response durations usually exceeding 1 year for patients with heavily pretreated, relapsed disease.</li>

4282<li>

4283Nivolumab was well tolerated by patients and can be used to achieve a clinical complete remission before autologous or allogeneic SCT.</li>

4284<li>

4285The FDA approved nivolumab for use after both relapse from SCT and previous exposure to brentuximab vedotin. Nivolumab is also approved if the patient has received three different previous treatments, including SCT.</li>

4286</ul>

4287</div>

4288</li>

4289<li>

4290In a phase I/II study of 62 patients with relapsed or refractory HL, the combination of nivolumab and brentuximab vedotin was well tolerated (&lt;10% of patients required systemic steroids). The combination resulted in an 82% objective response rate and a 61% complete response rate, allowing patients to proceed to an autologous SCT.[<a href="#cit/section_8.13">

429113</a>

4292][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810039&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810039&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

4293Level of evidence C3</a>

4294]</li>

4295</ol>

4296</div>

4297</section>

4298<section id="_1047">

4299<h4 id="_1047_toc">

4300Brentuximab vedotin</h4>

4301<p id="_1048" tabindex="-1">

4302Brentuximab vedotin is an antibody-drug conjugate directed against CD30.[<a href="#cit/section_8.14">

430314</a>

4304-<a href="#cit/section_8.16">

430516</a>

4306] CD30 is a target for therapy because it is expressed on malignant Reed-Sternberg cells of HL but has limited expression on normal cells. Brentuximab vedotin is well tolerated by patients and can be used to achieve a clinical complete response before autologous or allogeneic SCT.</p>

4307<p id="_1049" tabindex="-1">

4308Evidence (brentuximab vedotin):</p>

4309<div class="pdq-content-list">

4310<ol id="_1050">

4311<li>

4312In multiple trials for patients with relapsed disease, including one trial performed after allogeneic SCT, the following results were observed:<div class="pdq-content-list">

4313<ul id="_1051">

4314<li>

4315For patients with relapsing disease, response rates were approximately 75%. Complete remission rates were approximately 50% and median PFS was 4 to 8 months.[<a href="#cit/section_8.14">

431614</a>

4317-<a href="#cit/section_8.18">

431818</a>

4319][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810039&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810039&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

4320Level of evidence C3</a>

4321] </li>

4322</ul>

4323</div>

4324</li>

4325<li>

4326Twenty-seven previously untreated patients older than 60 years, judged by the investigator to be in poor condition and unable to undergo chemotherapy, received brentuximab vedotin.[<a href="#cit/section_8.19">

432719</a>

4328]<div class="pdq-content-list">

4329<ul id="_1052">

4330<li>

4331A 92% overall response rate and 73% complete remission rate were reported.[<a href="#cit/section_8.19">

433219</a>

4333][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810039&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810039&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

4334Level of evidence C3</a>

4335]</li>

4336</ul>

4337</div>

4338</li>

4339<li>

4340Retreatment with brentuximab vedotin was successful in patients with relapsed disease, with a response rate of 60%.[<a href="#cit/section_8.20">

434120</a>

4342][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810039&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810039&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

4343Level of evidence C3</a>

4344]</li>

4345<li>

4346For 329 patients at high risk of residual HL after SCT, the double-blind <a href="https://clinicaltrials.gov/ct2/show/NCT01100502" title="https://clinicaltrials.gov/ct2/show/NCT01100502">

4347AETHERA</a>

4348 trial (NCT01100502) evaluated brentuximab vedotin versus placebo.[<a href="#cit/section_8.21">

434921</a>

4350,<a href="#cit/section_8.22">

435122</a>

4352]<div class="pdq-content-list">

4353<ul id="_1053">

4354<li>

4355With a median follow-up of 5.0 years, the 5-year PFS rate for brentuximab vedotin was 59% (95% CI, 51%&#8211;66%) versus 41% (95% CI, 33%&#8211;49%) for placebo (HR, 0.521; 95% CI, 0.379&#8211;0.717).[<a href="#cit/section_8.21">

435621</a>

4357,<a href="#cit/section_8.22">

435822</a>

4359][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

4360Level of evidence B1</a>

4361]</li>

4362<li>

4363The 16-month treatment duration after transplant was not achieved by most patients because they developed progressive peripheral neuropathy, which was partially reversible after discontinuation of brentuximab vedotin.</li>

4364</ul>

4365</div>

4366</li>

4367<li>

4368In two phase I/II studies, 120 patients with relapsed or refractory HL received brentuximab vedotin and bendamustine.[<a href="#cit/section_8.23">

436923</a>

4370]<div class="pdq-content-list">

4371<ul id="_1197">

4372<li>

4373After two cycles, the objective response rates were 93% and 78%, and the complete remission rates were 74% and 32%.[<a href="#cit/section_8.23">

437423</a>

4375,<a href="#cit/section_8.24">

437624</a>

4377][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810039&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810039&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

4378Level of evidence C3</a>

4379]</li>

4380</ul>

4381</div>

4382</li>

4383</ol>

4384</div>

4385</section>

4386<section id="_1283">

4387<h4 id="_1283_toc">

4388Brentuximab vedotin plus nivolumab</h4>

4389<p id="_1284" tabindex="-1">

4390Evidence (brentuximab vedotin plus nivolumab):</p>

4391<div class="pdq-content-list">

4392<ol id="_1285">

4393<li>

4394In a phase II trial, 91 patients with relapsed or refractory HL received brentuximab vedotin and nivolumab.[<a href="#cit/section_8.25">

439525</a>

4396] Prior brentuximab vedotin therapy was allowed if the patient was not resistant or intolerant to the drug.<div class="pdq-content-list">

4397<ul id="_1286">

4398<li>

4399With a median follow-up of 34.3 months, the overall response rate was 85%, and the complete response rate was 67%. The 3-year PFS rate was 77% (95% CI, 65%&#8211;86%) for all patients and 91% (95% CI, 79%&#8211;96%) for those who received autologous SCT. The 3-year OS rate was 93% (95% CI, 85%&#8211;97%).[<a href="#cit/section_8.25">

440025</a>

4401][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810039&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810039&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

4402Level of evidence C3</a>

4403]</li>

4404<li>

4405In this trial, 16% of patients had adverse events that required treatment with steroids.</li>

4406</ul>

4407</div>

4408</li>

4409</ol>

4410</div>

4411</section>

4412<section id="_1083">

4413<h4 id="_1083_toc">

4414Chemotherapy with stem cell transplant</h4>

4415<p id="_1084" tabindex="-1">

4416Patients whose HL relapses after initial

4417combination chemotherapy can undergo reinduction with the same or another

4418chemotherapy regimen followed by high-dose chemotherapy and autologous bone

4419marrow or peripheral stem cell or allogeneic bone marrow rescue.[<a href="#cit/section_8.1">

44201</a>

4421,<a href="#cit/section_8.26">

442226</a>

4423-<a href="#cit/section_8.29">

442429</a>

4425] This

4426therapy has resulted in 3- to 4-year DFS rates of up to 50%. Patients who are responsive to reinduction therapy may have a better

4427prognosis after subsequent autologous SCT; in one analysis, the 3-year event-free survival (EFS) rate was 80% with negative PET-CT scan results and 29% with positive PET-CT scan results.[<a href="#cit/section_8.30">

442830</a>

4429]</p>

4430<p id="_1085" tabindex="-1">

4431Patients who do not respond to induction chemotherapy (about 20%&#8210;25% of all presenting patients) have survival rates lower than 10% at 8 years.[<a href="#cit/section_8.3">

44323</a>

4433] For these patients, high-dose chemotherapy and autologous bone marrow or peripheral stem cell or allogeneic bone marrow rescue [<a href="#cit/section_8.26">

443426</a>

4435,<a href="#cit/section_8.27">

443627</a>

4437,<a href="#cit/section_8.31">

443831</a>

4439-<a href="#cit/section_8.33">

444033</a>

4441] have resulted in 5-year DFS rates of around 25% to 30%, but selection bias clearly influences these numbers.[<a href="#cit/section_8.26">

444226</a>

4443,<a href="#cit/section_8.27">

444427</a>

4445,<a href="#cit/section_8.32">

444632</a>

4447,<a href="#cit/section_8.34">

444834</a>

4449,<a href="#cit/section_8.35">

445035</a>

4451]</p>

4452<p id="_1086" tabindex="-1">

4453In a retrospective review of 105 patients, those older than 60 years fared better with a combination of chemotherapy and salvage radiation therapy than with the use of intensified transplant consolidation.[<a href="#cit/section_8.36">

445436</a>

4455][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810039&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810039&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

4456Level of evidence C3</a>

4457]</p>

4458<p id="_1087" tabindex="-1">

4459The use of HLA-matched sibling marrow (allogeneic transplant) results

4460in lower relapse rates, but the benefit may be offset by increased toxic

4461effects.[<a href="#cit/section_8.26">

446226</a>

4463,<a href="#cit/section_8.37">

446437</a>

4465,<a href="#cit/section_8.38">

446638</a>

4467] Reduced-intensity conditioning for allogeneic SCT is also under clinical evaluation.[<a href="#cit/section_8.39">

446839</a>

4469-<a href="#cit/section_8.41">

447041</a>

4471]</p>

4472<p id="_1088" tabindex="-1">

4473Evidence (chemotherapy with SCT):</p>

4474<div class="pdq-content-list">

4475<ol id="_1089">

4476<li>

4477A randomized trial compared aggressive conventional chemotherapy versus high-dose chemotherapy with autologous hematopoietic SCT for relapsed chemosensitive HL.[<a href="#cit/section_8.42">

447842</a>

4479][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

4480Level of evidence B1</a>

4481]<div class="pdq-content-list">

4482<ul id="_1090">

4483<li>

4484This trial showed improvement in freedom from treatment failure at 3 years for the transplant arm (55%) versus the chemotherapy-alone arm (34%).[<a href="#cit/section_8.42">

448542</a>

4486]</li>

4487<li>

4488No difference was observed in overall survival (OS).</li>

4489</ul>

4490</div>

4491</li>

4492<li>

4493A Cochrane meta-analysis concluded that autologous SCT after reinduction chemotherapy improves relapse-free survival by 20% to 30% over chemotherapy alone, but without an OS benefit.[<a href="#cit/section_8.43">

449443</a>

4495][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

4496Level of evidence B1</a>

4497]</li>

4498<li>

4499In three retrospective reviews of patients who

4500underwent autologous bone marrow transplant (ABMT) for relapsed or refractory disease, a comparison was made between

4501those who received involved-field radiation therapy (IFRT) for residual masses after

4502high-dose therapy and those who received no further treatment.[<a href="#cit/section_8.44">

450344</a>

4504-<a href="#cit/section_8.46">

450546</a>

4506]<div class="pdq-content-list">

4507<ul id="_1091">

4508<li>

4509Those who received

4510IFRT had decreased local disease recurrence.</li>

4511<li>

4512Normalization of fluorine F 18-fludeoxyglucose PET-CT scans after reinduction therapy predicted a much better outcome after SCT, with an EFS rate of 80% versus 29% in one phase II trial.[<a href="#cit/section_8.30">

451330</a>

4514][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810037&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810037&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

4515Level of evidence C2</a>

4516]</li>

4517</ul>

4518</div>

4519</li>

4520</ol>

4521</div>

4522<p id="_1092" tabindex="-1">

4523After completion of autologous SCT for recurrent HL, 329 patients were randomly assigned to receive brentuximab vedotin or placebo in a double-blind trial (<a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT01100502">

4524AETHERA</a>

4525 [NCT01100502]).[<a href="#cit/section_8.21">

452621</a>

4527,<a href="#cit/section_8.22">

452822</a>

4529]</p>

4530<div class="pdq-content-list">

4531<ul id="_1093">

4532<li>

4533With a median follow-up of 5.0 years, the 5-year PFS rate for brentuximab vedotin was 59% (95% CI, 51%&#8211;66%) versus 41% (95% CI, 33%&#8211;49%) for placebo (HR, 0.521; 95% CI, 0.379&#8211;0.717).[<a href="#cit/section_8.21">

453421</a>

4535,<a href="#cit/section_8.22">

453622</a>

4537][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

4538Level of evidence B1</a>

4539]</li>

4540<li>

4541The 16-month treatment duration after transplant was not achieved by most patients because they developed progressive peripheral neuropathy, which was partially reversible after discontinuation of brentuximab vedotin.</li>

4542<li>

4543It is unclear whether the results of this trial are applicable when brentuximab vedotin is employed before transplant, such as during reinduction after relapse or during initial therapy (presently under clinical evaluation).</li>

4544</ul>

4545</div>

4546<p id="_1094" tabindex="-1">

4547A phase II trial reported a response rate higher than 50% for bendamustine in relapsing ABMT patients.[<a href="#cit/section_8.47">

454847</a>

4549][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810039&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810039&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

4550Level of evidence C3</a>

4551] For patients with recurrent disease after ABMT, weekly

4552vinblastine therapy has provided palliation with minimal toxic

4553effects.[<a href="#cit/section_8.48">

455448</a>

4555][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810039&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810039&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

4556Level of evidence C3</a>

4557]</p>

4558</section>

4559<section id="_933">

4560<h4 id="_933_toc">

4561Combination chemotherapy</h4>

4562<p id="_834" tabindex="-1">

4563For patients who experience a relapse after initial

4564combination chemotherapy, prognosis is determined more by the duration of the

4565first remission than by the specific induction or salvage combination

4566chemotherapy regimen. Patients whose initial remission after chemotherapy was

4567longer than 1 year (late relapse) have long-term survival rates of 22% to 71% with salvage

4568chemotherapy.[<a href="#cit/section_8.2">

45692</a>

4570-<a href="#cit/section_8.4">

45714</a>

4572,<a href="#cit/section_8.49">

457349</a>

4574-<a href="#cit/section_8.51">

457551</a>

4576] Patients whose initial remission after

4577chemotherapy was shorter than 1 year (early relapse) do much worse and have

4578long-term survival rates of 11% to 46%.[<a href="#cit/section_8.2">

45792</a>

4580,<a href="#cit/section_8.3">

45813</a>

4582,<a href="#cit/section_8.52">

458352</a>

4584]</p>

4585<p id="_1075" tabindex="-1">

4586It is rare to see a patient who received only radiation therapy for initial treatment, but patients who experience a relapse after initial wide-field, high-dose radiation

4587therapy have a good prognosis. Combination chemotherapy results in 10-year

4588DFS rates of 57% to 81% and OS rates of 57% to 89%.[<a href="#cit/section_8.2">

45892</a>

4590,<a href="#cit/section_8.53">

459153</a>

4592-<a href="#cit/section_8.55">

459355</a>

4594]</p>

4595</section>

4596<section id="_937">

4597<h4 id="_937_toc">

4598Radiation therapy</h4>

4599<p id="_177" tabindex="-1">

4600For the small subgroup of patients with only limited nodal recurrence following

4601initial chemotherapy, radiation therapy with or without additional chemotherapy

4602may provide long-term survival for about 50% of these highly selected patients.[<a href="#cit/section_8.56">

460356</a>

4604,<a href="#cit/section_8.57">

460557</a>

4606]</p>

4607</section>

4608<section id="_1076">

4609<h4 id="_1076_toc">

4610Summary for sequencing therapies for recurrent classic HL</h4>

4611<div class="pdq-content-list">

4612<ul id="_1079">

4613<li>

4614Start with pembrolizumab or nivolumab alone, brentuximab vedotin alone, or the combination of a checkpoint inhibitor plus brentuximab vedotin. If clinical complete remission is achieved, proceed to autologous SCT.</li>

4615<li>

4616Chemotherapy with ICE (ifosfamide, carboplatin, etoposide) or GVD remain as options. If chemotherapy results in inadequate response, proceed to pembrolizumab (or nivolumab).</li>

4617<li>

4618Consider allogeneic SCT for patients with primary refractory disease who achieved partial response or complete remission on salvage therapy.</li>

4619</ul>

4620</div>

4621</section>

4622</section>

4871 <section id="_1104">

4872

4873 <h2>

4874Treatment of Nodular Lymphocyte–Predominant HL (NLPHL)</h2>

4875

4876 <div id="_section_1104" class="pdq-sections">

4877<nav class="in-this-section" role="navigation">

4878<h6>

4879In This Section</h6>

4880<ul>

4881<li>

4882<a href="#_1108_toc">

4883Treatment Options for NLPHL<ul>

4884<li>

4885<a href="#_1250_toc">

4886Watchful waiting/active surveillance</a>

4887</li>

4888<li>

4889<a href="#_1111_toc">

4890Radiation therapy</a>

4891</li>

4892<li>

4893<a href="#_1114_toc">

4894Chemotherapy</a>

4895</li>

4896<li>

4897<a href="#_1117_toc">

4898Rituximab</a>

4899</li>

4900</ul>

4901</a>

4902</li>

4903<li>

4904<a href="#_1119_toc">

4905Follow-Up</a>

4906</li>

4907<li>

4908<a href="#_TrialSearch_1104_sid_9_toc">

4909Current Clinical Trials</a>

4910</li>

4911</ul>

4912</nav>

4913<p id="_1105" tabindex="-1">

4914Immunophenotypic differences distinguish NLPHL (CD15-, CD20+, CD30-) from lymphocyte-rich classic Hodgkin lymphoma (HL) (CD15+, CD20-, CD30+).[<a href="#cit/section_9.1">

49151</a>

4916,<a href="#cit/section_9.2">

49172</a>

4918] The largest retrospective report of 426 cases showed no significant difference in clinical response or outcome to standard therapies for these two subgroups when patients present with early-stage disease (stage I or II).[<a href="#cit/section_9.3">

49193</a>

4920][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810035&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810035&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

4921Level of evidence C1</a>

4922] </p>

4923<p id="_1106" tabindex="-1">

4924Patients with NLPHL have earlier-stage disease and longer survival than those with classic HL.[<a href="#cit/section_9.4">

49254</a>

4926,<a href="#cit/section_9.5">

49275</a>

4928] NLPHL is usually diagnosed in asymptomatic younger patients with cervical or inguinal lymph nodes; this usually occurs without mediastinal involvement. Unlike patients with classic HL, bulky disease, B symptoms, and contiguous spread are uncommon in patients with NLPHL.[<a href="#cit/section_9.6">

49296</a>

4930,<a href="#cit/section_9.7">

49317</a>

4932]</p>

4933<section id="_1108">

4934<h3 id="_1108_toc">

4935Treatment Options for NLPHL</h3>

4936<p id="_1109" tabindex="-1">

4937Treatment options for NLPHL include the following:</p>

4938<div class="pdq-content-list">

4939<ol id="_1110">

4940<li>

4941<a href="/types/lymphoma/hp/adult-hodgkin-treatment-pdq#_1250">

4942Watchful waiting/active surveillance</a>

4943.</li>

4944<li>

4945<a href="/types/lymphoma/hp/adult-hodgkin-treatment-pdq#_1111">

4946Radiation therapy (early stage)</a>

4947.</li>

4948<li>

4949<a href="/types/lymphoma/hp/adult-hodgkin-treatment-pdq#_1114">

4950Chemotherapy (advanced stage)</a>

4951.</li>

4952<li>

4953<a href="/types/lymphoma/hp/adult-hodgkin-treatment-pdq#_1117">

4954Rituximab</a>

4955.</li>

4956</ol>

4957</div>

4958<section id="_1250">

4959<h4 id="_1250_toc">

4960Watchful waiting/active surveillance</h4>

4961<p id="_1251" tabindex="-1">

4962Because of the favorable prognosis for NLPHL and the potential long-term side effects of therapy, studies have evaluated watchful waiting or active surveillance for patients with asymptomatic, low tumor burden disease.[<a href="#cit/section_9.8">

49638</a>

4964] In a retrospective comparison, 37 such patients managed with active surveillance had a 5-year progression-free survival (PFS) rate of 77%, versus 85% for patients receiving active treatment.[<a href="#cit/section_9.9">

49659</a>

4966][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810039&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810039&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

4967Level of evidence C3</a>

4968]</p>

4969</section>

4970<section id="_1111">

4971<h4 id="_1111_toc">

4972Radiation therapy</h4>

4973<p id="_1112" tabindex="-1">

4974Limited-field radiation therapy is the most-common treatment approach for patients with early-stage disease. This histology is rare, but this approach is based on retrospective analysis spanning several decades.[<a href="#cit/section_9.5">

49755</a>

4976,<a href="#cit/section_9.10">

497710</a>

4978-<a href="#cit/section_9.14">

497914</a>

4980]</p>

4981<p id="_1113" tabindex="-1">

4982Patients with nonbulky lymphocyte&#8211;predominant disease presenting in unilateral

4983high neck (above the thyroid notch) or epitrochlear locations require only

4984involved-field radiation therapy (IFRT) after clinical staging.[<a href="#cit/section_9.15">

498515</a>

4986] A retrospective report

4987of 426 cases of lymphocyte-predominant HL (including the

4988nodular lymphocyte&#8211;predominant and lymphocyte-rich classic

4989subtypes) showed that more patients died of acute and long-term treatment-related toxicity than of recurrent HL.[<a href="#cit/section_9.3">

49903</a>

4991][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810035&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810035&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

4992Level of evidence C1</a>

4993] Limitation of radiation dose and radiation fields and avoidance of

4994leukemogenic chemotherapeutic agents, along with watchful waiting policies,

4995should be investigated for these subgroups.[<a href="#cit/section_9.14">

499614</a>

4997,<a href="#cit/section_9.16">

499816</a>

4999]</p>

5000</section>

5001<section id="_1114">

5002<h4 id="_1114_toc">

5003Chemotherapy</h4>

5004<p id="_1115" tabindex="-1">

5005For patients with early-stage NLPHL, ABVD (doxorubicin, bleomycin, vinblastine, and dacarbazine) for two to three cycles has been combined with IFRT on the basis of anecdotal single-arm trials.[<a href="#cit/section_9.5">

50065</a>

5007,<a href="#cit/section_9.17">

500817</a>

5009]</p>

5010<p id="_1116" tabindex="-1">

5011For patients with advanced-stage NLPHL, chemotherapy regimens designed for patients with non-Hodgkin lymphomas, such as R-CHOP (rituximab, cyclophosphamide, doxorubicin, vincristine, and prednisone) or R-CVP (rituximab, cyclophosphamide, vincristine, and prednisone), may be preferred, based on two retrospective reviews and a phase II study.[<a href="#cit/section_9.7">

50127</a>

5013,<a href="#cit/section_9.18">

501418</a>

5015-<a href="#cit/section_9.20">

501620</a>

5017][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810039&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810039&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

5018Level of evidence C3</a>

5019]</p>

5020</section>

5021<section id="_1117">

5022<h4 id="_1117_toc">

5023Rituximab</h4>

5024<p id="_1118" tabindex="-1">

5025In a phase II trial of 39 patients with previously untreated and relapsed NLPHL, most of whom had advanced-stage disease, treatment with rituximab yielded a 100% response rate. With a median follow-up of 9.8 years, the median PFS was 3.0 years for patients who received rituximab induction only and 5.6 years for patients who received rituximab induction plus rituximab maintenance.[<a href="#cit/section_9.21">

502621</a>

5027][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810037&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810037&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

5028Level of evidence C2</a>

5029] With induction only, 9 of 23 patients had disease relapse with an aggressive B-cell lymphoma.</p>

5030</section>

5031</section>

5032<section id="_1119">

5033<h3 id="_1119_toc">

5034Follow-Up</h3>

5035<p id="_1120" tabindex="-1">

5036Despite a usually favorable prognosis, there is a tendency for histological transformation of NLPHL to diffuse large B-cell lymphoma or T-cell&#8211;rich large B-cell lymphoma in approximately 10% of patients by 10 years.[<a href="#cit/section_9.6">

50376</a>

5038,<a href="#cit/section_9.21">

503921</a>

5040,<a href="#cit/section_9.22">

504122</a>

5042] This propensity of NLPHL to transform to aggressive B-cell lymphoma underscores the importance of long-term follow-up and rebiopsy at relapse.[<a href="#cit/section_9.21">

504321</a>

5044,<a href="#cit/section_9.23">

504523</a>

5046]</p>

5047<p id="_1121" tabindex="-1">

5048With a median

5049follow-up of 7 to 8 years, more patients died of treatment-related toxic

5050effects (acute and long-term) than of recurrent HL. Limitation of

5051radiation dose and fields and avoidance of leukemogenic chemotherapeutic

5052agents, along with watchful waiting policies, should be investigated for these

5053subgroups.[<a href="#cit/section_9.5">

50545</a>

5055,<a href="#cit/section_9.16">

505616</a>

5057,<a href="#cit/section_9.24">

505824</a>

5059]</p>

5060<p id="_1122" tabindex="-1">

5061The treatment approach for relapsing disease is similar to that for recurrent follicular lymphoma. Based on age and performance status, some patients receive sequential therapies and watchful waiting, and some patients receive aggressive salvage chemoimmunotherapy (like R-ICE [rituximab, ifosfamide, carboplatin, and etoposide]) followed by stem cell transplant.[<a href="#cit/section_9.7">

50627</a>

5063,<a href="#cit/section_9.25">

506425</a>

5065,<a href="#cit/section_9.26">

506626</a>

5067]</p>

5068</section>

5069<section id="_TrialSearch_1104_sid_9">

5070<h3 id="_TrialSearch_1104_sid_9_toc">

5071Current Clinical Trials</h3>

5072<p id="_TrialSearch_1104_22" tabindex="-1">

5073Use our <a href="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/treatment/clinical-trials/search/advanced" title="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/treatment/clinical-trials/search/advanced">

5074advanced clinical trial search</a>

5075 to find NCI-supported cancer clinical trials that are now enrolling patients. The search can be narrowed by location of the trial, type of treatment, name of the drug, and other criteria. <a href="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/treatment/clinical-trials/" title="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/treatment/clinical-trials/">

5076General information</a>

5077 about clinical trials is also available.</p>

5078</section>

5197
