5227<section id="_449">

5228<h3 id="_449_toc">

5229Introduction</h3>

5230<p id="_450" tabindex="-1">

5231Hodgkin lymphoma (HL) affects primarily young women, some of whom may be pregnant. When treating a pregnant woman, an oncologist will provide therapy that minimizes risk to the fetus. Treatment choice must be individualized,

5232taking into consideration the following:</p>

5233<div class="pdq-content-list">

5234<ul id="_957">

5235<li>

5236The mother&#8217;s wishes.</li>

5237<li>

5238The severity and aggressiveness of the

5239HL.</li>

5240<li>

5241The trimester of the pregnancy.</li>

5242</ul>

5243</div>

5244</section>

5245<section id="_451">

5246<h3 id="_451_toc">

5247Stage Information for HL During Pregnancy</h3>

5248<p id="_452" tabindex="-1">

5249To avoid exposing a pregnant woman to ionizing

5250radiation, magnetic resonance imaging

5251is the preferred method for staging evaluation.[<a href="#cit/section_10.1">

52521</a>

5253] The presenting stage, clinical behavior, prognosis, and histological subtypes of HL in pregnant women do not differ from those in nonpregnant women during their childbearing years.[<a href="#cit/section_10.2">

52542</a>

5255] For more information, see the <a href="/types/lymphoma/hp/adult-hodgkin-treatment-pdq#_12">

5256Stage Information for HL</a>

5257 section.</p>

5258</section>

5259<section id="_453">

5260<h3 id="_453_toc">

5261Treatment Options for HL During Pregnancy</h3>

5262<p id="_851" tabindex="-1">

5263Treatment options for HL during pregnancy include the following:</p>

5264<div class="pdq-content-list">

5265<ol id="_938">

5266<li>

5267Watchful waiting.</li>

5268<li>

5269Radiation therapy.</li>

5270<li>

5271Chemotherapy.</li>

5272</ol>

5273</div>

5274<p id="_916" tabindex="-1">

5275In one study, the 20-year survival rate of pregnant women with HL did not differ from the 20-year survival rate of nonpregnant women who were matched for similar stage of disease, age at diagnosis, and calendar year of treatment.[<a href="#cit/section_10.3">

52763</a>

5277] </p>

5278<p id="_981" tabindex="-1">

5279The long-term effects on progeny after chemotherapy in utero are unknown, although evidence seems promising.[<a href="#cit/section_10.3">

52803</a>

5281-<a href="#cit/section_10.7">

52827</a>

5283]</p>

5284<p id="_982" tabindex="-1">

5285Based on anecdotal series, there is no evidence that a pregnancy after completion of therapy increases the relapse rate for patients in remission.[<a href="#cit/section_10.8">

52868</a>

5287,<a href="#cit/section_10.9">

52889</a>

5289]</p>

5290<section id="_853">

5291<h4 id="_853_toc">

5292Therapy during the first trimester</h4>

5293<p id="_454" tabindex="-1">

5294HL that is diagnosed in the first trimester of pregnancy does not constitute an absolute indication for therapeutic abortion. Treatment options for each patient must take into account disease stage, rapidity of growth of the lymphoma, and the patient's wishes.[<a href="#cit/section_10.10">

529510</a>

5296] </p>

5297<section id="_983">

5298<h5 id="_983_toc">

5299Watchful waiting</h5>

5300<p id="_984" tabindex="-1">

5301If the HL presents in

5302early stage above the diaphragm and is growing slowly, patients can

5303be observed carefully, with plans to induce delivery early and proceed with

5304definitive therapy.[<a href="#cit/section_10.11">

530511</a>

5306]</p>

5307</section>

5308<section id="_985">

5309<h5 id="_985_toc">

5310Radiation therapy</h5>

5311</section>

5312<p id="_854" tabindex="-1">

5313Alternatively, these patients can receive radiation

5314therapy with proper shielding.[<a href="#cit/section_10.12">

531512</a>

5316-<a href="#cit/section_10.15">

531715</a>

5318] Investigators at the MD Anderson Cancer Center reported no

5319congenital abnormalities in 16 babies delivered after the mothers had received

5320supradiaphragmatic radiation while the uterus was shielded with five half-value

5321layers of lead.[<a href="#cit/section_10.16">

532216</a>

5323] Because of theoretical risks of the fetus developing future malignancies from even minimal scattered radiation doses outside the radiation field, postponing radiation therapy&#8212;if possible, until after delivery&#8212;should be considered.[<a href="#cit/section_10.17">

532417</a>

5325]</p>

5326<section id="_986">

5327<h5 id="_986_toc">

5328Chemotherapy</h5>

5329</section>

5330<p id="_987" tabindex="-1">

5331Evidence (chemotherapy during the first trimester):</p>

5332<div class="pdq-content-list">

5333<ol id="_988">

5334<li>

5335Chemotherapy that is administered in the first trimester has been

5336associated with congenital abnormalities in as many as 33% of infants.[<a href="#cit/section_10.4">

53374</a>

5338,<a href="#cit/section_10.18">

533918</a>

5340]

5341Consequently, some

5342women may opt to continue the pregnancy and agree to radiation therapy or

5343chemotherapy if immediate treatment is required after the first trimester.</li>

5344<li>

5345A multicenter retrospective analysis of 40 patients described pregnancy termination in 3 patients, deferral of therapy to postpartum in 13 patients (median 30-week gestation), and antenatal therapy applied to the remaining 24 patients (median 21-week gestation, all done after the first trimester).[<a href="#cit/section_10.19">

534619</a>

5347]<div class="pdq-content-list">

5348<ul id="_989">

5349<li>

5350With a median follow-up of 41 months, the 3-year progression-free survival (PFS) rate was 85%, and the overall survival (OS) rate was 97%, often with the use of ABVD (doxorubicin, bleomycin, vinblastine, and dacarbazine).[<a href="#cit/section_10.19">

535119</a>

5352][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810039&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810039&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

5353Level of evidence C3</a>

5354]</li>

5355</ul>

5356</div>

5357</li>

5358<li>

5359A retrospective analysis of 39 patients from the MD Anderson Cancer Center described pregnancy termination in 3 patients, deferral of therapy to the postpartum period in 12 patients, and antenatal therapy applied to 24 patients.[<a href="#cit/section_10.20">

536020</a>

5361]<div class="pdq-content-list">

5362<ul id="_990">

5363<li>

5364Two women miscarried after receiving doxorubicin-based chemotherapy in the first trimester.</li>

5365<li>

5366With a median follow-up of 68 months from diagnosis, the 5-year PFS rate was 75%, and the OS rate was 82%. These rates did not differ between the antenatal and postpartum timing of therapy.[<a href="#cit/section_10.20">

536720</a>

5368][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810039&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810039&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

5369Level of evidence C3</a>

5370] </li>

5371</ul>

5372</div>

5373</li>

5374</ol>

5375</div>

5376</section>

5377<section id="_855">

5378<h4 id="_855_toc">

5379Therapy later in pregnancy</h4>

5380<section id="_991">

5381<h5 id="_991_toc">

5382Watchful waiting</h5>

5383<p id="_992" tabindex="-1">

5384In the second half of pregnancy, patients can be observed carefully,

5385and therapy can be postponed until induction of delivery at 32 to 36 weeks.[<a href="#cit/section_10.6">

53866</a>

5387,<a href="#cit/section_10.7">

53887</a>

5389,<a href="#cit/section_10.18">

539018</a>

5391]</p>

5392</section>

5393<section id="_994">

5394<h5 id="_994_toc">

5395Radiation therapy</h5>

5396<p id="_856" tabindex="-1">

5397As an

5398alternative, a short course of radiation therapy can be used before delivery in

5399cases of respiratory compromise caused by a rapidly enlarging mediastinal mass.</p>

5400</section>

5401<section id="_993">

5402<h5 id="_993_toc">

5403Chemotherapy</h5>

5404<p id="_456" tabindex="-1">

5405 If

5406chemotherapy is mandatory before delivery&#8212;such as for patients with

5407symptomatic advanced-stage disease&#8212;vinblastine alone, given intravenously at 6 mg/m&#178; every 2 weeks until induction of delivery, may

5408be considered because it has not been associated with fetal abnormalities in the

5409second half of pregnancy.[<a href="#cit/section_10.6">

54106</a>

5411,<a href="#cit/section_10.7">

54127</a>

5413] Combination chemotherapy with ABVD appears to be safe in the second half of pregnancy.[<a href="#cit/section_10.5">

54145</a>

5415] If chemotherapy is required after the first trimester, many clinicians prefer the combination of drugs over single-agent drugs or radiation therapy. Steroids are employed both for their

5416antitumor effect and for hastening fetal pulmonary maturity.</p>

5417</section>

5418</section>

5419</section>

5512 <h2>

5513Changes to This Summary (08/04/2023)</h2>

5514

5515 <div id="_section_207" class="pdq-sections">

5516<p id="_208" tabindex="-1">

5517The PDQ cancer information summaries are reviewed regularly and updated as

5518new information becomes available. This section describes the latest

5519changes made to this summary as of the date above.</p>

5520<p id="_1331" tabindex="-1">

5521<strong>

5522<a href="/types/lymphoma/hp/adult-hodgkin-treatment-pdq#_1">

5523General Information About Hodgkin Lymphoma (HL)</a>

5524</strong>

5525</p>

5526<p id="_1332" tabindex="-1">

5527Added <a href="/types/lymphoma/hp/adult-hodgkin-treatment-pdq#_762">

5528text</a>

5529 to state that risk prediction models found that mediastinal radiation therapy combined with doxorubicin exposure conferred the highest risk of cardiac disease, followed by mediastinal radiation therapy alone.</p>

5530<p id="_1333" tabindex="-1">

5531<strong>

5532<a href="/types/lymphoma/hp/adult-hodgkin-treatment-pdq#_12">

5533Stage Information for HL</a>

5534</strong>

5535</p>

5536<p id="_1334" tabindex="-1">

5537Added <a href="/types/lymphoma/hp/adult-hodgkin-treatment-pdq#_881">

5538text</a>

5539 to state that an updated clinical prediction model for patients with advanced HL uses continuous variables listed for the International Prognostic Index, with an online calculator available (cited Rodday et al. as reference 14).</p>

5540<p id="_1335" tabindex="-1">

5541<strong>

5542<a href="/types/lymphoma/hp/adult-hodgkin-treatment-pdq#_373">

5543Treatment of Early Unfavorable Classic HL</a>

5544</strong>

5545</p>

5546<p id="_1336" tabindex="-1">

5547Added <a href="/types/lymphoma/hp/adult-hodgkin-treatment-pdq#_1130">

5548text</a>

5549 about the results of a prospective phase II trial of patients with early-stage bulky disease who received ABVD for two cycles, followed by an interim PET scan, with further therapy based on the PET results (cited LaCasce et al. as reference 16 and level of evidence C3).</p>

5569 <section id="_AboutThis_1">

5570

5571 <h2>

5572About This PDQ Summary</h2>

5573

5574 <div id="_section_AboutThis_1" class="pdq-sections">

5575<section id="_AboutThis_2">

5576<h3 id="_AboutThis_2_toc">

5577Purpose of This Summary</h3>

5578<p id="_AboutThis_3" tabindex="-1">

5579This PDQ cancer information summary for health professionals provides comprehensive, peer-reviewed, evidence-based information about the treatment of adult Hodgkin lymphoma. It is intended as a resource to inform and assist clinicians in the care of their patients. It does not provide formal guidelines or recommendations for making health care decisions.</p>

5580</section>

5581<section id="_AboutThis_4">

5582<h3 id="_AboutThis_4_toc">

5583Reviewers and Updates</h3>

5584<p id="_AboutThis_5" tabindex="-1">

5585This summary is reviewed regularly and updated as necessary by the <a href="https://www.cancer.gov/publications/pdq/editorial-boards/adult-treatment" title="https://www.cancer.gov/publications/pdq/editorial-boards/adult-treatment">

5586PDQ Adult Treatment Editorial Board</a>

5587, which is editorially independent of the National Cancer Institute (NCI). The summary reflects an independent review of the literature and does not represent a policy statement of NCI or the National Institutes of Health (NIH).</p>

5588<p id="_AboutThis_22" tabindex="-1">

5589 Board members review recently published articles each month to determine whether an article should:</p>

5590<div class="pdq-content-list">

5591<ul id="_AboutThis_6">

5592<li>

5593be discussed at a meeting,</li>

5594<li>

5595be cited with text, or</li>

5596<li>

5597replace or update an existing article that is already cited.</li>

5598</ul>

5599</div>

5600<p id="_AboutThis_7" tabindex="-1">

5601Changes to the summaries are made through a consensus process in which Board members evaluate the strength of the evidence in the published articles and determine how the article should be included in the summary.</p>

5602<p id="" tabindex="-1">

5603The lead reviewer for Hodgkin Lymphoma Treatment is:</p>

5604<div class="pdq-content-list">

5605<ul id="">

5606<li>

5607Eric J. Seifter, MD (Johns Hopkins University)</li>

5608</ul>

5609</div>

5610<p id="_AboutThis_9" tabindex="-1">

5611Any comments or questions about the summary content should be submitted to Cancer.gov through the NCI website's <a href="https://www.cancer.gov/contact/email-us" title="https://www.cancer.gov/contact/email-us">

5612Email Us</a>

5613. Do not contact the individual Board Members with questions or comments about the summaries. Board members will not respond to individual inquiries.</p>

5614</section>

5615<section id="_AboutThis_10">

5616<h3 id="_AboutThis_10_toc">

5617Levels of Evidence</h3>

5618<p id="_AboutThis_11" tabindex="-1">

5619Some of the reference citations in this summary are accompanied by a level-of-evidence designation. These designations are intended to help readers assess the strength of the evidence supporting the use of specific interventions or approaches. The PDQ Adult Treatment Editorial Board uses a <a href="/publications/pdq/levels-evidence/treatment">

5620formal evidence ranking system</a>

5621 in developing its level-of-evidence designations.</p>

5622</section>

5623<section id="_AboutThis_12">

5624<h3 id="_AboutThis_12_toc">

5625Permission to Use This Summary</h3>

5626<p id="_AboutThis_13" tabindex="-1">

5627PDQ is a registered trademark. Although the content of PDQ documents can be used freely as text, it cannot be identified as an NCI PDQ cancer information summary unless it is presented in its entirety and is regularly updated. However, an author would be permitted to write a sentence such as &#8220;NCI&#8217;s PDQ cancer information summary about breast cancer prevention states the risks succinctly: [include excerpt from the summary].&#8221;</p>

5628<p id="_AboutThis_14" tabindex="-1">

5629The preferred citation for this PDQ summary is:</p>

5630<p id="_AboutThis_15" tabindex="-1">

5631PDQ&#174; Adult Treatment Editorial Board. PDQ Hodgkin Lymphoma Treatment. Bethesda, MD: National Cancer Institute. Updated &lt;MM/DD/YYYY&gt;. Available at: <a href="https://www.cancer.gov/types/lymphoma/hp/adult-hodgkin-treatment-pdq" title="https://www.cancer.gov/types/lymphoma/hp/adult-hodgkin-treatment-pdq">

5632https://www.cancer.gov/types/lymphoma/hp/adult-hodgkin-treatment-pdq</a>

5633. Accessed &lt;MM/DD/YYYY&gt;. [PMID: 26389473]</p>

5634<p id="_AboutThis_16" tabindex="-1">

5635Images in this summary are used with permission of the author(s), artist, and/or publisher for use within the PDQ summaries only. Permission to use images outside the context of PDQ information must be obtained from the owner(s) and cannot be granted by the National Cancer Institute. Information about using the illustrations in this summary, along with many other cancer-related images, is available in <a href="https://visualsonline.cancer.gov/" title="https://visualsonline.cancer.gov/">

5636Visuals Online</a>

5637, a collection of over 2,000 scientific images.

5638

5639</p>

5640</section>

5641<section id="_AboutThis_17">

5642<h3 id="_AboutThis_17_toc">

5643Disclaimer</h3>

5644<p id="_AboutThis_18" tabindex="-1">

5645Based on the strength of the available evidence, treatment options may be described as either &#8220;standard&#8221; or &#8220;under clinical evaluation.&#8221; These classifications should not be used as a basis for insurance reimbursement determinations. More information on insurance coverage is available on Cancer.gov on the <a href="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/managing-care" title="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/managing-care">

5646Managing Cancer Care</a>

5647 page.</p>
